<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136712766 space=MD2024x version=1 -->
## PAGE 01386: Viewing and analyzing differences of modified diagrams

- page_id: `136712766`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136712766/Viewing+and+analyzing+differences+of+modified+diagrams
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:14:51.308+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Model analysis > Comparing projects > Analyzing comparison results
- labels: ['analyzing-changes', 'difference-viewer', 'comparison-result']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The different diagram versions are displayed in separate **Difference Viewer** tabs in the **Difference Viewer** window next to the **Differences** tree (see the following figure).

To open diagram difference viewers of a modified diagram

- Double-click the modified diagram in the Differences tree.

One, two or three new tabs open in the **Difference Viewer** window. The base tab is opened by default. If a diagram is only available in compared, only this tab is opened in the difference viewer.

All the diagram difference viewers are used to display the following changes:

- One or more symbols were moved or modified on the diagram.
- A new symbol was added to the diagram.
- A symbol was deleted from the diagram.
- The number of inner model elements has changed.
- A model element has been modified.

Be advised that symbols with property value changes that actually have no effect on their appearance are highlighted in a diagram difference viewer as well. For example, changing the **Show Stereotypes** property value in the **Symbol Properties** dialog of a class makes the class symbol highlighted as changed in a diagram difference viewer.

Asyou can see in the following figure, all these changes are marked by color coded lines and flags allowing the quick distinguishing between different types of changes. Numbers on flags indicate the number of changes made to that element. Clicking a flag switches to the **Differences**tab and selects the flagged element in the **Differences** tree.

The colors of lines and flags correspond to the color system explained in the difference legend:

- Blue flags indicate the number of modification/movement changes made to the element, blue lines represent modified/moved relations, and blue borders around symbols mark modified/moved elements in the diagram.
- Green flags indicate the number of addition changes made to the element, green lines represent added relations, and green borders around symbols mark added elements in the diagram.
- Red flags indicate the number of deletion changes made to the element, red lines represent deleted relations, and red borders around symbols mark deleted elements in the diagram.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

You can customize the types of changes you want to be displayed in the difference viewer by using filtering options available in the legend. Simply select or clear selection from the appropriate check-boxes and view the differences that are relevant to you. 
 [IMAGE alt='' src='']

If you would like to see the diagram version from other project version without switching between tabs, use the slider available at the bottom of the **Difference Viewer**. Moving the slider makes the current diagram symbols to fade, and the symbols from another diagram version start appearing. When the slider is set to the middle position, different symbols from both diagram.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

You can manage the content of a diagram difference viewer using the toolbar that is located above it. 
 [IMAGE alt='' src='']

See the button descriptions in the following table.

| Button | Tooltip text | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Return to Merged Result | Click to open the Differences tree with the appropriate diagram selected within. |
|  | Synchronize Zooming | Click to turn on or off the zooming synchronization in all difference viewers of the same diagram. |
|  | Synchronize Scrolling | Click to turn on or off scrolling synchronization in all difference viewers of the same diagram. |
|  | Print Diagram | Click the button to print a diagram. The diagram will be printed with highlighted areas on it, if the highlighting of the diagram changes is turned on. |
|  | Zooming | Use the buttons to control the diagram size. |

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>The different diagram versions are displayed in separate <strong>Difference Viewer</strong> tabs in the <strong>Difference Viewer</strong> window next to the <strong>Differences</strong> tree (s<span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">ee the following figure)</span>.</p><p> </p><p>To open diagram difference viewers of a modified diagram</p><hr /><ul><li>Double-click the modified diagram in the <strong>Differences</strong> tree.</li></ul><p>One, two or three new tabs open in the <strong>Difference Viewer</strong> window. The base tab is opened by default. If a diagram is only available in compared, only this tab is opened in the difference viewer.</p><p>All the diagram difference viewers are used to display the following changes:</p><ul><li>One or more symbols were moved or modified on the diagram.</li><li>A new symbol was added to the diagram.</li><li>A symbol was deleted from the diagram.</li><li>The number of inner model elements has changed.</li><li>A model element has been modified.</li></ul><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="377a4e1e-54e0-46ab-b728-1a1b016810a2"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Be advised that symbols with property value changes that actually have no effect on their appearance are highlighted in a diagram difference viewer as well. For example, changing the <strong>Show Stereotypes</strong> property value in the <strong>Symbol Properties</strong> dialog of a class makes the class symbol highlighted as changed in a diagram difference viewer.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">As </span>you can see in the following figure, all these changes are marked by color coded lines and flags allowing the quick distinguishing between different types of changes. Numbers on flags indicate the number of changes made to that element. Clicking a flag switches to the <strong>Differences </strong>tab and selects the flagged element in the <strong>Differences</strong> tree.</p><p><ac:inline-comment-marker ac:ref="244e86a6-66d8-4636-86b6-9c6d8998af98">The colors of lines and flags correspond to the color system explained in the difference legend</ac:inline-comment-marker>:</p><ul><li>Blue flags indicate the number of modification/movement changes made to the element, blue lines represent modified/moved relations, and blue borders around symbols mark modified/moved elements in the diagram.</li><li>Green flags indicate the number of addition changes made to the element, green lines represent added relations, and green borders around symbols mark added elements in the diagram.</li><li>Red flags indicate the number of deletion changes made to the element, red lines represent deleted relations, and red borders around symbols mark deleted elements in the diagram.</li></ul><p><ac:image ac:title="Project Compare difference viewer" ac:alt="Project Compare difference viewer"><ri:attachment ri:filename="comparer_difference_viewer.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Viewing and analyzing differences of modified diagrams" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p> </p><p>You can customize the types of changes you want to be displayed in the difference viewer by using filtering options available in the legend. Simply select or clear selection from the appropriate check-boxes and view the differences that are relevant to you.<br /> <ac:image ac:border="true" ac:title="Difference viewer legend and change slider" ac:alt="Difference viewer legend and change slider" ac:height="42" ac:width="595"><ri:attachment ri:filename="difference_viewer_legend.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Viewing and analyzing differences of modified diagrams" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p> </p><p>If you would like to see the diagram version from other project version without switching between tabs, use the slider available at the bottom of the <strong>Difference Viewer</strong>. Moving the slider makes the current diagram symbols to fade, and the symbols from another diagram version start appearing. When the slider is set to the middle position, different symbols from both diagram.</p><p><ac:image ac:border="true" ac:title="Difference slider" ac:alt="Difference slider" ac:height="44" ac:width="306"><ri:attachment ri:filename="comparer_slider.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Viewing and analyzing differences of modified diagrams" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p> </p><p>You can manage the content of a diagram difference viewer using the toolbar that is located above it. <br class="atl-forced-newline" /> <ac:image <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136713479 space=MD2024x version=2 -->
````
## PAGE 01387: Viewing project history

- page_id: `136713479`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136713479/Viewing+project+history
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2023-12-12T14:22:08.530+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Collaborative modeling > Collaboration powered by 3DEXPERIENCE platform
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

After logging in to the **3D**EXPERIENCE****platform, you can view the version history of any project on the server. You can not only see who made changes to a project and when they were made, but also open a historical version of the project.

To view project history

1. Do one of the following:
  - In the main menu of a modeling tool, select Collaborate > Projects .
  - In the main menu of a modeling tool, select Collaborate > Open Server Project .
2. In the open dialog, select the project whose history you want to view and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the dialog toolbar. The **History** dialog opens displaying the project version history. [IMAGE alt='' src=''] Viewing version propertiesTo view the properties of a specific project version, in the **History** dialog, select a project version and click the **Properties** button. The **Version Properties** dialog opens displaying project version details, such as the commit comment, used projects, and the list of programs and plugins required to open the project.

##### Opening historic project versions

You can open and view a historic project version in a modeling tool as described below. However, historic project versions cannot be edited, updated, or committed to the server.

To open a historic project version

1. Do one of the following:
  - In the main menu of a modeling tool, select Collaborate > Projects .
  - In the main menu of a modeling tool, select Collaborate > Open Server Project .
2. In the open dialog, select the project whose historical version you want to open and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the dialog toolbar.
3. In the History dialog, select the version you want to open an click the Open button. [ATTACHMENT filename='opening_historical_version.png']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>After logging in to the <strong>3D</strong>EXPERIENCE<strong> </strong>platform, you can view the version history <span style="color: rgb(62,63,64);">of any project on the server. ## PAGE 01388: Viewing Version Properties
````

- page_id: `160760379`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/160760379/Viewing+Version+Properties
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-03-05T09:37:07.444+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Collaborative modeling > Using Teamwork Cloud > Managing server projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The **Version Properties** dialog shows project version information, for example, comments, tags, modules, and meta information.

To open the Version Properties dialog

1. From the Collaborate menu, select Open Server Project or Projects... .
2. Select a project and click the [ATTACHMENT filename='version_properties.png'] button on the Collaboration toolbar. OR Right-click a project and select Version Properties. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
3. In the Version Properties dialog, you can:
  - View the project author, version number, and creation date with the time zone: [ATTACHMENT filename='version_properties_project_info.png']
  - View project comments in the Comment tab.
  - Add the Major tag in the Tags tab to set the selected project as the major version: [ATTACHMENT filename='tags_version_properties.png']
  - View used projects in the Used Projects tab.
  - Select the Meta information tab to see which programs and plugins are required to open the selected project: [ATTACHMENT filename='meta_information.png']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE


<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136715162 space=MD2024x version=2 -->
## PAGE 01389: Visitors

- page_id: `136715162`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136715162/Visitors
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2024-02-13T08:08:06.017+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > Developer Guide > UML model > Working with UML model > Model traversing, Visitor pattern
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Visitor design pattern is implemented in UML model structure. Every *com.nomagic.uml2.ext.magicdraw.classes.mdkernel.Element* has the *accept(**AbstractVisitor)*method for visiting it*.*

The *com.nomagic.uml2.impl.ModelVisitor* has the *visit<element_metatype>*method for all types of model elements. This is very useful when you are working with a large collection of elements**and need to perform actions, specific for every type of *Element*(for example, save/load, copy/paste, or a specific properties setting).

Just derive your class from *com.nomagic.magicdraw.uml.InheritanceVisitor* and override some *visit...*methods and call *accept(**AbstractVisitor)* for *Elements.*

```java
it = root.getOwnedElement().iterator();
    while (it.hasNext())
    {
        it.next().accept(myVisitor);
    }]]>
```

****You can find the code examples in *<installation_directory>\openapi\examples\statistics*

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<ac:layout><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_right_sidebar"><ac:layout-cell><p>Visitor design pattern is implemented in UML model structure. Every <em>com.nomagic.uml2.ext.magicdraw.classes.mdkernel.Element</em> has the <em>accept(</em><em>AbstractVisitor) </em>method for visiting it<em style="line-height: 1.4285715;">. </em></p><p>The <em>com.nomagic.uml2.impl.ModelVisitor</em> has the <em>visit&lt;element_metatype&gt; </em>method for all types of model elements. This is very useful when you are working with a large collection of elements<em style="line-height: 1.4285715;"> </em>and need to perform actions, specific for every type of <em style="line-height: 1.4285715;">Element </em>(for example, save/load, copy/paste, or a specific properties setting).</p><p>Just derive your class from <em>com.nomagic.magicdraw.uml.InheritanceVisitor</em> and override some <em>visit... </em>methods and call <em>accept(</em><em>AbstractVisitor)</em> for <em>Elements.</em></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="code" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="79f767f1-b453-4cbc-823c-e1689c691119"><ac:parameter ac:name="language">java</ac:parameter><ac:plain-text-body><![CDATA[    ModelVisitor myVisitor = new ModelVisitor()
    {
        // override some visit methods ...

        {
        	//this is my UML Class 
        }
    };
    Project project = ...;
    Package root = project.getPrimaryModel(); 
    Iterator<Element> it = root.getOwnedElement().iterator();
````

## PAGE 01390: Web Publisher 2.0 report

- page_id: `136714123`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136714123/Web+Publisher+2.0+report
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:16:09.177+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Report Wizard > Generating Reports from Report Wizard
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Note

347568349

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Note

347568351

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Note

347568350

Web Publisher 2.0 is a Java-Doc-like report template with a clickable navigation and an image map for all diagrams and elements. It allowsyou to publish MagicDraw models (including diagrams) in HTML with rich features, and to open them using your browser, e.g., Microsoft Edge, Opera, or Firefox.

This section describes the features of Web Publisher 2.0, illustrates how to generate a Web Publisher 2.0 report template by using the Magic Library.mdzip sample project, and gives you examples on how to work with each feature.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### A Web Publisher 2.0 report.

#### NOTE: Note

Note

Web Publisher 2.0 report is not fully supported by Google Chrome (unless following the steps below), Opera, and Microsoft Edge (Chromium-based); therefore, the data tree structure in the Containment tree may be missing because they do not allow JavaScript to load local files via **XMLHttpRequest**. You can solve this problem by doing one of the following:

- Deploy Web Publisher 2.0 report on web server, or
- Start Google Chrome with " --allow-file-access-from-files " argument by following the steps below:
  1. Close the web browser (Chrome) instances.
  2. Open the web browser with " --allow-file-access-from-files " argument. 2.1 Right click on web browser launcher and select Properties .

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

2.2 Add this argument "**--allow-file-access-from-files**" next to the web browser installation path.

###### [IMAGE alt='' src='']

2.3 Open the web browser instance from the launcher.

2.4 Open the generated Web 2.0 report.

2.5 Start the web browser from the launcher or command line that contains "**--allow-file-access-from-files**" argument before.

#### NOTE: Note

Note

Web Publisher 2.0 report is also supported by Firefox. You can configure Firefox before opening Web Publisher 2.0 report by doing the following:

1. In the Firefox address box, type about:config . [ATTACHMENT filename='config.png']
2. Find the security.fileuri.strict_origin_policy parameter and set its parameter value to false .

#### NOTE: Note

Note

You can also open Web Publisher 2.0 on Safari by doing the following:

1. Open Safari.
2. On the toolbar of the browser, click Safari and select Preferences . The Preference dialog opens.
3. Click the Advanced tab and select the Show Develop menu in menu bar option. Close the dialog. [ATTACHMENT filename='Safari Preference Advanced Dialog.png']
4. On the toolbar of the browser, click Develop and select Disable Local File Restrictions .

Safari is now able to open Web Publisher 2.0.

#### NOTE: Note

Note

In Report Wizard 2021x Refresh 2 and later, **$exporter2 (DOM : Exporter2)** is no longer used, and **$exporter3(XMLStream : ExporterTool3)** is used by default instead.

If you want to continue using Exporter2, use the following line in *index.html* of the Web Publisher 2.0 template:

```text

```

Cameo Collaborator is developed for replacing Web Publisher Collaboration report. This is a web-based solution for publishing and reviewing models online. See more detail at [Cameo Collaborator for Teamwork Cloud Documentation](https://www.3ds.com/products-services/catia/products/no-magic/cameo-collaborator-for-teamwork-cloud/)

347568348

**Related pages**

argument before.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="6d397470-695b-400e-a7b2-c25dd09c32ba"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Note</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>Web Publisher 2.0 report is also supported by Firefox.  You can configure Firefox before opening Web Publisher 2.0 report by doing the following:</p><ol><li>In the Firefox address box, type <strong>about:config</strong>.<br /><br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="config.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Web Publisher 2.0 report" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /><br /></li><li>Find the <strong>security.fileuri.strict_origin_policy</strong> parameter and set its parameter value to <strong>false</strong>.</li></ol></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="afebbfc6-1ea8-4b03-8601-7c75a7c65a56"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Note</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>You can also open Web Publisher 2.0 on Safari by doing the following:</p><ol><li>Open Safari.</li><li>On the toolbar of the browser, click <strong>Safari</strong> and select <strong>Preferences</strong>. The Preference dialog opens.</li><li>Click the <strong>Advanced</strong> tab and select the <strong>Show Develop menu in menu bar</strong> option. Close the dialog.<br /><br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="Safari Preference Advanced Dialog.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Web Publisher 2.0 report" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /><br /></li><li>On the toolbar of the browser, click <strong>Develop</strong> and select <strong>Disable Local File Restrictions</strong>.</li></ol><p>Safari is now able to open Web Publisher 2.0.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="1f21522f-f183-4810-80ad-7459588add25"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Note</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>In Report Wizard 2021x Refresh 2 and later, <strong>$exporter2 (DOM : Exporter2)</strong> is no longer used, and <strong>$exporter3(XMLStream : ExporterTool3)</strong> is used by default instead.</p><p>If you want to continue using Exporter2, use the following line in <em>index.html</em> of the Web Publisher 2.0 template:</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="code" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="bb83dadc-d0df-4ebf-b07e-ba106357622e"><ac:parameter ac:name="language">text</ac:parameter><ac:plain-text-body><![CDATA[XMLRequest.send('$exporter2.exportAll(true, $linkedFile)', renderBrowser);]]></ac:plain-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p>Cameo Collaborator is developed for replacing Web Publisher Collaboration report. This is a web-based solution for publishing and reviewing models online. See more detail at <a href="https://www.3ds.com/products-services/catia/products/no-magic/cameo-collaborator-for-teamwork-cloud/">Cameo Collaborator for Teamwork Cloud Documentation</a></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="d8fa182a-8527-4cf7-9954-6dc11f237cea"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">347568348</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><strong>Related pages</strong></p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="children" ac:schema-version="2" ac:macro-id="72500a1f-e65d-4d46-90c8-87b0347b80fd" /></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro>

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136714519 space=MD2024x version=1 -->
## PAGE 01391: What is a Template?

- page_id: `136714519`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136714519/What+is+a+Template
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:16:38.998+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Report Wizard > Template Creation Tutorial > Introduction
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

A template, in Velocity, is a text file that tells Velocity what the output should look like. It contains a document page style, layout, header, footer, and static text just like any other template that comes with most of the Word Processor programs. However, a Velocity template also contains specific placeholders for Java objects and Velocity Template Language scripts which will tell the Velocity Engine what and how to print the information in the output.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>A template, in Velocity, is a text file that tells Velocity what the output should look like. It contains a document page style, layout, header, footer, and static text just like any other template that comes with most of the Word Processor programs. However, a Velocity template also contains specific placeholders for Java objects and Velocity Template Language scripts which will tell the Velocity Engine what and how to print the information in the output.</p>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136710006 space=MD2024x version=1 -->
## PAGE 01392: Why is prototyping so important?

- page_id: `136710006`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136710006/Why+is+prototyping+so+important
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:12:20.624+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Diagrams > Extension diagrams > User Interface Modeling diagram
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Various versions of User Interfaces are tested to see how clients respond. Client response is important for main dialogs, such as a sign-up screen for a website or an e-commerce application. Working with User Interface prototypes instead of "real" User Interfaces enables you to work with small details (such as color or the position of a button), as well as a substantially reduced designer and programmer overhead in the design phase. By building mock-ups or prototypes, you receive fast feedback from prospective users for future designs. User Interface prototyping makes this possible. The feedback loop makes for quicker sophisticated designs that work for everybody, which is what matters.

You can build mock-ups or prototypes to meet the following objectives:

- Integrate GUI development with UML specifications. Since this is a new field with increased design capability, it is easier to see the missing parts in UML or User Interface modeling.
- Enable business analysts to quickly gather requirements via permanent feedback from prospective users, making it easier to obtain all the information needed.
- Create browsable User Interface prototypes/ GUI simulation/ Story-boarding. Several prototypes can be connected via hyperlinks with one another and then be presented together in a report to simulate the workflow of an application.
- Resolve flow issues. It is easier to think through a problem when a User-related Interface can be changed quickly.
- Get "buy-in" from stakeholders. A visual representation of a particular User Interface can be shown more rapidly.
- Run a usability test before full production so that potential errors in usability, like overfilled screens or a usage too complicated, can be avoided.
- Test a series of interaction widgets. Consider, for example, that another text field or button would be good on a screen. Since modifying a prototype is easy, it is much simpler to present these suggestions to others.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>Various versions of User Interfaces are tested to see how clients respond. Client response is important for main dialogs, such as a sign-up screen for a website or an e-commerce application. Working with User Interface prototypes instead of &quot;real&quot; User Interfaces enables you to work with small details (such as color or the position of a button), as well as a substantially reduced designer and programmer overhead in the design phase. By building mock-ups or prototypes, you receive fast feedback from prospective users for future designs. User Interface prototyping makes this possible. The feedback loop makes for quicker sophisticated designs that work for everybody, which is what matters.</p><p>You can build mock-ups or prototypes to meet the following objectives:</p><ul><li>Integrate GUI development with UML specifications. Since this is a new field with increased design capability, it is easier to see the missing parts in UML or User Interface modeling.</li><li>Enable business analysts to quickly gather requirements via permanent feedback from prospective users, making it easier to obtain all the information needed.</li><li>Create browsable User Interface prototypes/ GUI simulation/ Story-boarding. Several prototypes can be connected via hyperlinks with one another and then be presented together in a report to simulate the workflow of an application.</li><li>Resolve flow issues. It is easier to think through a problem when a User-related Interface can be changed quickly.</li><li>Get &quot;buy-in&quot; from stakeholders. A visual representation of a particular User Interface can be shown more rapidly.</li><li>Run a usability test before full production so that potential errors in usability, like overfilled screens or a usage too complicated, can be avoided.</li><li>Test a series of interaction widgets. Consider, for example, that another text field or button would be good on a screen. Since modifying a prototype is easy, it is much simpler to present these suggestions to others.</li></ul>
````

## PAGE 01393: Working with Actions

- page_id: `136710851`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136710851/Working+with+Actions
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:13:03.086+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Action
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

907190545

907190548

907190547

To create any action quickly

1. In the Activity diagram toolbar , right-click or expand the Action button. The menu opens. [ATTACHMENT filename='action_toolbar.png']
2. Select the Any Action command. The Select Action Metaclass dialog opens. [ATTACHMENT filename='select_action_metaclass.png']
3. Select an Action metaclass from the list, or type the first letter of the metaclass in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Quick filter' space='MD2024x']. Click **OK**. The Action is created.
4. Click the diagram pane. An action symbol is drawn.

##### Applying duration constraint on the Action

You can create and apply a duration constraint on an Action that states that the output must occur after delay from the input.

To create and apply a duration constraint

1. Select an Action and create the input and output [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Pin' space='MD2024x'] to specify the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Event' space='MD2024x'] .
2. Create a duration constraint for the Action using one of the following way:
  - From the diagram palette:
    1. In the diagram palette, under the Common category, expand the Constraint command, and select the Duration Constraint, Time Constraint, or Constraint button, and create it directly on the action shape.
  - In the Specification window: 
 a. In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024x'] [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024x'], click the **Constraints** group. 
 b. Click the **Apply** button. The **Select Constraint** dialog opens. 
 c. Select the constraint storage place, and click the **Create** button. In the opened menu, select the **Duration Constraint** command. The **Duration Constraint** Specification window opens.
3. Specify a duration interval. Type the minimum and maximum duration to hold the Activity in the Min and Max property specification cells, e.g., 0 sec and 30 sec.
4. Assign the Events for the input and output pins:
  1. In the opened **Duration Constraint** Specification window, click the **Specification** property specification cell, and click the Show Shortcut Menu button [IMAGE alt='' src='']. The following shortcut menu opens: [IMAGE alt='' src='']
  2. Select the **Open Specification** command. The **Duration Interval** Specification window opens.
  3. Click the **Min** property specification cell, and and click the Show Shortcut Menu button [IMAGE alt='' src='']. In the shortcut menu, select the **Open Specification** command. The **Duration** Specification window opens.
  4. In the Event field, click the “...” button. The **Select Element** dialog opens. Select the activity input pin.
  5. Repeat steps c and d for the Max property - select the action output pin as an event.
5. Apply the created duration constraint on the action.

The following sample depicts a fragment of the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Activity diagram' space='MD2024x'] with a duration constraint applied on the Action.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

## PAGE 01394: Working with Activity diagram

##### Behavior Creation Mode

You can use the **Behavior Creation Mode** to automatically create an Activity after creating a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024x'] in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with Activity diagram' space='MD2024x']. The newly created Activity will be set as the behavior of the Call Behavior Action.

To turn on the **Behavior Creation Mode** in an Activity diagram

- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Understanding the user interface' space='MD2024x'], click [IMAGE alt='' src='']. The****Behavior Creation Mode works separatelyfor each project.

When the **Behavior Creation Mode** is on:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Behavior' space='MD2024x']A Behavior is created together with the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024x']. It inherits the type of the Call Behavior Action owner.
- If a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024x'] and its [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Behavior' space='MD2024x'] are not titled, type a name on the Call Behavior Action shape on the diagram, and the typed name will be set as the Behavior's name automatically.

##### Creating Actions by pasting the copied list

You can copy the item list from the text editor (Word, Notepad, etc.), web page, PDF file, PowerPoint slide and paste it in the Activity diagram to create actions.

To create Actions by pasting items from the list

1. Copy the list.
2. Go to the diagram and press Ctrl+V.
3. Select an Action.
4. In the question dialog click Yes if you need to connect the Actions with Control Flow relationship.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Smart layout

###### Dynamiccenterlines

The centerlines are displayed only when the center of the shape that was moved or newly drawn is located near the center of a preexisting shape in the diagram. These lines help you to easily align shapes when drawing a diagram.

When the center of the shape that was moved coincides with a center of any shape that is placed to its right or left, a horizontal centerline appears. When the center of the shape is close to any center of a shape that is located above or below it, a vertical centerline appears.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To switch off the dynamic centerlines

- Click the Show Centerlines button [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the diagram toolbar, or press C .
- From the Options main menu, select Environment . In the Environment Options dialog, click the Diagram category, and clear the Show Centerlines in Flow Diagrams check box in the Display properties group.

###### Diagram orientation

The diagram orientation is used to assign the correct rectilinear path breaks and draw paths between the Activity diagram shapes. The paths can be drawn from side to side, or from the lower to the upper shape borders.

#### TIP: Example

Example

If you have a vertical diagram orientation and shapes are not in the same centerline, the paths will be connected from the lower border of the first shape to the upper border of the next shape, adding break points: 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
 
If you have a horizontal diagram orientation, the paths will be connected from the side border of the first shape to the next side border of the second shape, adding breakpoints: 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To change the diagram orientation

- From the Options main menu, select Project . In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Setting project options' space='MD2024x']**Project Options** dialog , expand Symbol Styles > Default > Diagram group (if it is not expanded by default) and, in the options list, change the value for the Diagram Orientation property.
- From the diagram pane shortcut menu, select Diagram Properties, or press Shift+Enter to open the Diagram Properties dialog. Change the value for the Diagram Orientation property in that dialog.

##### Deleting from Activity diagrams

- Note that after deleting the last symbol of an element from the Activity diagram, the element will be automatically removed from the model. This does not affect [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Pin' space='MD2024x'] and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Activity Parameter Node' space='MD2024x'] .
- If a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024x'] that has an assigned [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Behavior' space='MD2024x'] is deleted from the Activity diagram, then this Behavior is also deleted from the model.

This is valid if the assigned Behavior is editable and does not have more usages, i.e. there is not a Call Behavior Action that has a reference to this Behavior.

##### Displaying inner elements

To display inner elements

- When creating a new Activity diagram, right-click an Activity in the Containment tree, click Create Diagram , and then click Activity Diagram .

Inner elements are displayed on the Activity diagram pane automatically upon creating the first diagram under the Activity element.

- When modifying a previously created Activity diagram, select the diagram pane and do one of the following:

- From the shortcut menu, click**Display**>**Display Inner Elements**. 
- On the diagram toolbar click[IMAGE alt='' src=''],and select**Display Inner Elements**.

ac:name="atlassian-macro-output-type">INLINE</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ac:structured-macro ac:name="excerpt" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="ddd5f4a2-87c2-46db-ae0d-086fae3d8e47"><ac:parameter ac:name="atlassian-macro-output-type">INLINE</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><h3>Behavior Creation Mode</h3><p>You can use the <strong>Behavior Creation Mode</strong> to automatically create an Activity after creating a <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" /></ac:link> in the <ac:link><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Activity Diagram]]></ac:plain-text-link-body><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ac:link>. The newly created Activity will be set as the behavior of the Call Behavior Action.</p><p>To turn on the <strong>Behavior Creation Mode</strong> in an Activity diagram</p><hr /><ul><li><p class="auto-cursor-target">In the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Understanding the user interface" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[diagram palette]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>, click <span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image ac:title="Behavior Creation Mode" ac:alt="Behavior Creation Mode"><ri:attachment ri:filename="automatic_behavior_creation.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span>.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="8a792f8e-361c-4f23-8d0f-6accbb0243b6"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span><span class="confluence-link">The<strong> </strong>Behavior Creation Mode works <span><span class="confluence-link">separately </span></span>for each project.</span></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li></ul><p>When the <strong>Behavior Creation Mode</strong> is on:</p><ul><li><span><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Behavior" /><ac:link-body><span style="color: rgb(0,51,102);">A</span> Behavior</ac:link-body></ac:link> is created together with the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" /></ac:link>. It inherits the type of the Call Behavior Action owner.</span></li><li>If a <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" /></ac:link> and its <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Behavior" /></ac:link> are not titled, type a name on the Call Behavior Action shape on the diagram, and the typed name will be set as the Behavior's name automatically.</li></ul><h3 class="with-breadcrumbs">Creating Actions by pasting the copied list</h3><p><span style="color: rgb(62,63,64);">You can copy the item list from the text editor (Word, Notepad, etc.), web page, PDF file, PowerPoint slide and paste it in the Activity diagram to create actions.</span></p><p><br /></p><p>To create Actions by pasting items from the list</p><hr /><ol><li>Copy the list.</li><li>Go to the diagram and press Ctrl+V.</li><li>Select an Action.</li><li>In the question dialog click <strong>Yes</strong> if you need to connect the Actions with Control Flow relationship.</li></ol><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="paste_list_to_create_activities.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h3 class="with-breadcrumbs">Smart layout</h3><h4><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">Dynamic</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span>centerlines</h4><p>The centerlines are displayed only when the center of the shape that was moved or newly drawn is located near the center of a preexisting shape in the diagram. These lines help you to easily align shapes when drawing a diagram.</p><p>When the center of the shape that was moved coincides with a center of any shape that is placed to its right or left, a horizontal centerline appears. When the center of the shape is close to any center of a shape that is located above or below it, a vertical centerline appears.</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" /> <span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image ac:alt="Dynamic vertical centerline"><ri:attachment ri:filename="dynamic_centerline_vertical.gif"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p><p>To switch off the dynamic centerlines</p><hr /><ul><li>Click the <strong>Show Centerlines</strong> button <span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="show_centerlines.gif"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span> in the diagram toolbar, or press <strong>C</strong>.</li><li>From the <strong>Options</strong> main menu, select <strong>Environment</strong>. In the<strong> Environment Options</strong> dialog, click the <strong>Diagram</strong> category, and clear the <strong>Show Centerlines in Flow Diagrams</strong> check box in the <strong>Display</strong> properties group.</li></ul><p><br /></p><h4>Diagram orientation</h4><p>The diagram orientation is used to assign the correct rectilinear path breaks and draw paths between the Activity diagram shapes. The paths can be drawn from side to side, or from the lower to the upper shape borders.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="tip" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="c7b66ba1-861d-466b-a5e1-a9b825bb1752"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Example</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p> If you have a vertical diagram orientation and shapes are not in the same centerline, the paths will be connected from the lower border of the first shape to the upper border of the next shape, adding break points: <br class="atl-forced-newline" /><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="diagram_orientation_vertical.gif"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span><br class="atl-forced-newline" /><br class="atl-forced-newline" />If you have a horizontal diagram orientation, the paths will be connected from the side border of the first shape to the next side border of the second shape, adding breakpoints: <br class="atl-forced-newline" /><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="diagram_orientation_horizontal.gif"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper">To change the diagram orientation</span></p><hr /><ul><li>From the <strong>Options</strong> main menu, select <strong>Project</strong>. In the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Setting project options" /><ac:link-body><strong>Project Options</strong> dialog</ac:link-body></ac:link>, expand <strong>Symbol Styles </strong>&gt;<strong> Default </strong>&gt;<strong> </strong><strong>Diagram</strong> group (if it is not expanded by default) and, in the options list, change the value for the <strong>Diagram Orientation</strong> property.</li><li>From the diagram pane shortcut menu, select <strong>Diagram Properties,</strong> or press Shift+Enter to open the <strong>Diagram Properties</strong> dialog. Change the value for the <strong>Diagram Orientation</strong> property in that dialog.</li></ul><h3 class="with-breadcrumbs">Deleting from Activity diagrams</h3><ul><li>Note that after deleting the last symbol of an element from the Activity diagram, the element will be automatically removed from the model. This does not affect <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Pin" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Pins]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> and <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Activity Parameter Node" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Activity Parameter Nodes]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>.</li><li><p>If a <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" /></ac:link> that has an assigned <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Behavior" /></ac:link> is deleted from the Activity diagram, then this Behavior is also deleted from the model.</p></li></ul><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="d276b872-4811-4d21-98eb-dcfc6695d559"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span>This is valid if the assigned Behavior is editable and does not have more usages, i.e. there is not a Call Behavior Action that has a reference to this Behavior.</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Displaying inner elements</h3><p>To display inner elements</p><hr /><ul><li>When creating a new Activity diagram, right-click an Activity in the Containment tree, click <strong>Create Diagram</strong>, and then click <strong>Activity</strong><strong> </strong><strong>Diagram</strong>.</li></ul><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="43ea6a6d-d91c-48af-8008-72e4437c353a"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Inner elements are displayed on the Activity diagram pane automatically upon creating the first diagram under the Activity element.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ul><li><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper">When modifying a previously created Activity diagram, select the diagram pane and do one of the following:<br /></span></li></ul><p style="margin-left: ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>,</span><span> and select</span><strong> Display Inner Elements</strong><span>.</span><br <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136710878 space=MD2024x version=1 -->
## PAGE 01395: Working with Associations

- page_id: `136710878`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136710878/Working+with+Associations
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:13:04.439+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Association
- labels: ['reflective-association', 'association-class']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1018698642

1018698644

1018698643

An [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Association' space='MD2024x'] is a relationship between two classes. It is represented by a solid line. Though associations are bi-directional by default, they can also be unidirectional, where one class knows about the other class and the relationship but the other class does not. Sometimes an association links a class to itself. This association is called a recursive (reflexive) association. One example of this association is an employee who is managed by a manager who is also himself an employee.

To draw a recursive (reflexive) association

1. Select Association .
2. Click a class ( Employee in this example) and hover over the class until you see a rectangle shape. Click the class again to create a recursive association. [ATTACHMENT filename='recursiveAssociation.png']

##### Association Properties

You can specify association properties in the association [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024x']. The description of each property appears in the same window. The description area of the Specification window presents the descriptions.

To show the direction arrow near the association name

1. Do one of the following:
  - Right-click the association, and from the shortcut menu, select Show Direction Arrow .
  - Open the association [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Symbol Properties dialog' space='MD2024x'] dialog and set the Show Direction Arrow property to true .

The default Direction Arrow direction is displayed according to the path creation direction.

To change the **Direction Arrow** direction

1. Right-click the association.
2. From the shortcut menu, select Reverse Direction Arrow .

The Direction Arrow is a graphical representation most often used in top-level domain class diagrams. It helps to read a diagram and explains diagram semantics, and has no meaning in a model.

Usually, you would use the Direction Arrow on a diagram where navigability is not yet defined. Direction Arrows are usually displayed for named associations. When you create more detailed diagrams with specified navigability, direction arrows and association names are not usually displayed in these types of diagrams.

As shown in the following figure, *User* and *Account* Classes are connected with the Association. A navigation arrow can be displayed on either side depending on the Association name. If the association name is *belongs to*, the Direction Arrow should point from the *Account* to the *User*. If the Association name is *has*, the Direction Arrow should point from the *User* to the *Account*.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Examples of Direction Arrows

In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class diagram' space='MD2024x'], you can add [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Attribute' space='MD2024x'] to an Association using an [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Association Class' space='MD2024x']. The Association Class is a simple [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class' space='MD2024x']with a dashed line connected to the Association.

##### Adding Association between Read-Only Classifiers

Adding a new Association always creates two roles or properties at both ends. They are owned by the attached Classifier by default. However, when one or both ends of the Association are not editable (for example, locked in a server project or stored in a read-only profile or used project), the properties will be ownedby the Association itself. In this case, a warning appears informing you about any unexpected issue in model creation.

1018698641

**Related pages**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024x'] [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024x']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024x']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Customizing and Selecting Perspective' space='MD2024x']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136709501 space=MD2024x version=1 -->
## PAGE 01396: Working with attached files

- page_id: `136709501`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136709501/Working+with+attached+files
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:11:53.032+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with projects > Projects with file attachments
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The actions you can perform with attached files are listed below:

Attached files can also be included in reports. The attached file is saved in the file system together with the generated report. In this report, any hyperlink to that attached file defined in the model is replaced with reference to the appropriate file in the file system.

##### Modifying the contents

Attached files can be opened directly from MagicDraw and reviewed or modified with appropriate programs (documents – with MS Word, worksheets – with MS Excel, HTML files – with any HTML editor).

To open an attached file, do one of the following

- In the Containment tree, double-click the attached file.
- In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select Open File .
- Double-click either the element that has an active hyperlink to the attached file, or the shape of that element (see the following figure).

The file is opened in the appropriate program in your operating system. You can review or modify it.

[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
 
After closing the modified file, you can choose whether to save it in MagicDraw or not. Saving the latest version of the file in MagicDraw updates the **Modified** **At** property value of the appropriate Attached File element.

If the attached file is read-only, the changes made to it cannot be saved. To allow modifying the file, do one of the following:

- If the file is attached to used project, change the accessibility mode of this used project from read-only to read-write .
- If the file is attached to server project, lock the Attached File element for edit.

##### Inserting into HTML text

Attached image files can be inserted into HTML texts and displayed on diagrams. 
 
To insert an attached image file into HTML text

1. In the Containment tree, right-click the attached image file and select Copy Image URL .
2. On a diagram pane, draw a text box with the HTML mode on.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Advanced HTML Editor dialog' space='MD2024x']Open the **Advanced HTML Editor** dialog .
4. On the toolbar, click the Insert image button and select either:
  - From File button, then paste the URL into the Picture source field.
  - **From Attached File**button, then find and select the attached image file in the list. If you are working with a server project, make sure that the path to the image location is accessible from any computer that has Internet connection. Otherwise, the image won't be displayed, when the project is opened on another computer.
5. Click OK twice to close both the Picture Properties and Advanced HTML Editor dialogs.

The inserted image appears on the diagram. Now if you transfer the project to another computer, the diagram continues displaying the image. You can also insert images that are not yet attached to the project model. Read more about [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Inserting images into HTML text' space='MD2024x'][.](http://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024x/Inserting+an+image+into+HTML+text)

##### Exporting back to the local file system

To export the attached file back to the local file system

1. In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select**Save File As** .
2. Select the location in the local file system and click **Save**.

The file is saved in the local file system.

##### Creating image shapes

You can use attached imagefiles (*.gif*, *.jpg*, *.jpeg*, *.svg*, or *.png*) to create image shapes on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Understanding the user interface' space='MD2024x'].

To create an image shape using an attached image file

1. In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Containment tab' space='MD2024x'] select an already attached file or attach a new one. [How to attach a file in the Containment tree >>](https://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024x/Attaching%252C+reattaching%252C+and+detaching+files#Attaching,reattaching,anddetachingfiles-Attachingfiles) Image formatsYou can attach images of the following formats: *.gif*, *.jpg*, *.jpeg*, *.svg*, or *.png*.
2. Drag the attached file element to the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Understanding the user interface' space='MD2024x'].The image shape is created. Image does not updateImage shape is not synchronized with attached file. If you replace an image in the attached file, the image shape on the diagram pane will not update.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>The actions you can perform with attached files are listed below:</p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="toc" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="ff2ea14a-5e49-4318-87a0-9ad533580594" />    </p><p>Attached files can also be included in reports. The attached file is saved in the file system together with the generated report. In this report, any hyperlink to that attached file defined in the model is replaced with reference to the appropriate file in the file system.</p><h3>Modifying the contents</h3><p>Attached files can be opened directly from MagicDraw and reviewed or modified with appropriate programs (documents – with MS Word, worksheets – with MS Excel, HTML files – with any HTML editor).</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" />To open an attached file, do one of the following</p><hr /><ul><li>In the Containment tree, double-click the attached file.</li><li>In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select <strong>Open File</strong>.</li><li>Double-click either the element that has an active hyperlink to the attached file, or the shape of that element (see the following figure).</li></ul><p>The file is opened in the appropriate program in your operating system. You can review or modify it.</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" /><ac:image ac:border="true" ac:title="Element (left) and its shape (right) with active hyperlink to the attached file" ac:alt="Element (left) and its shape (right) with active hyperlink to the attached file" ac:height="68" ac:width="454"><ri:attachment ri:filename="active_hyperlink_to_attached_file.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with attached files" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br class="atl-forced-newline" /><br class="atl-forced-newline" />After closing the modified file, you can choose whether to save it in MagicDraw or not. Saving the latest version of the file in MagicDraw updates the <strong>Modified</strong> <strong>At</strong> property value of the appropriate Attached File element.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="05c871af-43a3-44e4-a88e-0ccb95217dcc"><ac:rich-text-body><p>If the attached file is read-only, the changes made to it cannot be saved. To allow modifying the file, do one of the following:</p><ul><li>If the file is attached to used project, change the accessibility mode of this used project from <em>read-only</em> to <em>read-write</em>.</li><li>If the file is attached to server project, lock the Attached File element for edit.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Inserting into HTML text</h3><p>Attached image files can be inserted into HTML texts and displayed on diagrams.<br class="atl-forced-newline" /><br class="atl-forced-newline" />To insert an attached image file into HTML text</p><hr /><ol><li>In the Containment tree, right-click the attached image file and select <strong>Copy Image URL</strong>.</li><li>On a diagram pane, draw a text box with the HTML mode on.</li><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Advanced HTML Editor dialog" /><ac:link-body>Open the <strong>Advanced HTML Editor</strong> dialog</ac:link-body></ac:link>.</li><li>On the toolbar, click the <strong>Insert image</strong> button and select either:<br /><br /><ul><li><strong>From File</strong> button, then paste the URL into the <strong>Picture source</strong> field.</li><li><p><strong>From Attached File </strong>button, then find and select the attached image file in the list.<br /><br /></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="2d581ff2-2ef7-4a34-923b-c4475947f5df"><ac:rich-text-body><p>If you are working with a server project, make sure that the path to the image location is accessible from any computer that has Internet connection. Otherwise, the image won't be displayed, when the project is opened on another computer.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p></li></ul></li><li>Click <strong>OK</strong> twice to close both the <strong>Picture Properties</strong> and <strong>Advanced HTML Editor</strong> dialogs.</li></ol><p>The inserted image appears on the diagram. Now if you transfer the project to another computer, the diagram continues displaying the image. You can also insert images that are not yet attached to the project model. Read more about <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Inserting images into HTML text" /></ac:link><a style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;" href="http://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024x/Inserting+an+image+into+HTML+text">.</a></p><h3>Exporting back to the local file system</h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To export the attached file back to the local file system</span></p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select<strong> Save File As</strong></span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Select the location in the local file system and click <strong>Save</strong>.</span></li></ol><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">The file is saved in the local file system.</span></p><h3><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">Creating image shapes</span></h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">You can use attached <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">image </span>files (<em>.gif</em>, <em>.jpg</em>, <em>.jpeg</em>, <em>.svg</em>, or <em>.png</em>) to create image shapes on the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Understanding the user interface" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[diagram pane]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>.</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To create an image shape using an attached image file<br /></span></p><hr /><ol><li><p class="auto-cursor-target"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Containment tab" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Containment tree]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> select an already attached file or attach a new one. <a href="https://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024x/Attaching%252C+reattaching%252C+and+detaching+files#Attaching,reattaching,anddetachingfiles-Attachingfiles">How to attach a file in the Containment tree &gt;&gt;</a><br /></span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="b358091b-36ab-4b19-bf3e-c86561895db6"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Image formats</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">You can attach images of the following formats: <em>.gif</em>, <em>.jpg</em>, <em>.jpeg</em>, <em>.svg</em>, or <em>.png</em>.</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p></li><li><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Drag the attached file element to the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Understanding the user interface" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[diagram pane]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>. </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">The image shape is created.</span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="81c9aecf-0a06-41e4-8c81-c3974cbc5eef"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Image does not update</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>Image shape is not synchronized with <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">attached file. If you replace an image in the attached file, the image shape on the diagram pane will not update. </span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p></li></ol>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=136712080 space=MD2024x version=1 -->
## PAGE 01397: Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard

- page_id: `136712080`
- space_key: `MD2024x`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024x/pages/136712080/Working+with+Automatic+Instantiation+Wizard
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2023-09-20T18:14:08.224+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Tools > Automatic Instantiation Wizard
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Note

907302760

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Note

907302781

907302758

**On this page**

3

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Note

907302771

You can create several different sets of instances using the **Automatic Instantiation** wizard. You can add each set to a different package and display it on a newly created diagram.

Depending on the size of your system, a very large number of instance specifications can be created using the wizard. That is why we strongly recommend selecting a new package wherein all created instance specifications will be stored.

##### Step #1. Selecting parts to be instantiated

In this step, you can see all the available instance specification values (parts) of your selected element. At this point, you can select which parts or properties to instantiate, create or select values for parts and properties, as well as add or remove parallel parts.

You can select/deselect the parts by clicking the check marks next to the parts or the options in the Selection area.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Parts are displayed if the multiplicity is greater than 1. The number of parts displayed depends on the multiplicity.

- If the multiplicity is a particular value, for example 2, then you will see 2 parts displayed in the **Automatic Instantiation**wizard. Also, in this case, you will not be able to add parallel parts or remove existing parallel parts.
- If the multiplicity is defined as an interval (for example, 0..*, 1..10, 1..* ) or *, only one part will be created by default. If you need more parts, you can create them by pressing **Insert** or selecting **Add parallel part** from the selected property’s shortcut menu.
- If the multiplicity is 1, parts will not be created.

The parts and properties are displayed with the suggested types, names, and values. In this step of the wizard, you can change them. You can also change the type for the part only if there is an available sub-element for that part in your model (see the Case study).

**Selecting a value for an instance**

To select a value for an instance

1. Select a part to be instantiated to which you want to add a value.
2. In **Instantiated properties**, click a **Value** specification cell and then click the ... button.
3. The **Select Instance Specification** dialog opens.
4. In the opened dialog, select the instance specification you want to add for the selected instance.
5. Click the **OK** button.

To create a value for an instance

1. Select a part to be instantiated for which you want to create a value.
2. In **Instantiated properties**, click the **Value** specification cell and then click the **Show Shortcut Menu** button. [IMAGE alt='' src='']
3. In the opened shortcut menu, point to the **Value Specification** and then select one of the available value types.
4. In the **Value property** specification cell, type the desired value. [IMAGE alt='' src='']

**Changing the name of an instance**

Each instance has a defaultname that uses the dot notation. However, you can change the default name by clicking the value row next to the **Name** property and typing the new name for the instance. ****

[IMAGE alt='' src=''] ****

**Applying a custom stereotypeto an instance**

You can also apply the custom stereotype to the instance. Only those stereotypes can be applied that have *Instance Specification* as their metaclass and whose customizations have a meta property named *classifier*with the **New Types** property value set to the instantiated element’s type.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The custom «ControllerFMU» and «ControllerSTM» stereotypes have *Instance Specification* as their metaclass 
and their respective customizations *ControllerFMU Customization* and *ControllerSTM Customization* have a meta property named classifier with the **New Types** property value set to the «Controller» stereotype. 
Since the *Controller* class has the «Controller» stereotype applied, the «ControllerFMU» and «ControllerSTM» stereotypes can be applied to the *Controller* class's instance.

**Changing a type for an instance**

You can change the type for the property's instance only if that type is a subtype of a Class (connected throughGeneralization). As shown in the following figure, the *Engine GM* Class and *Engine GMR C*lass are subtypes of the *Engine*Class. When creating an instance for the *Vehicle* Class, you can change the type of the *engine*Property by selecting one of the following: *Engine GM* Class, *Engine GMR* Class, or *Engine*Class.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Changing the type for a Part Property instance directly in the Automatic Instantiation dialog.

##### Step #2. Selecting a package

In this step, you can select the package to store instance specifications. You can select anexisting package from the element tree, create a new package, or clone selectedpackages. Click the **Finish** buttonafter this step if you do not want to display your created instance specifications.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To create a new Package in the element tree

1. In the element tree, select the Package for which you want to create the new one.
2. Click the **Creation Mode** button.
3. Click the **Create Owner** button.
4. From the open menu, select the package kind. The Specification window of that package opens.
5. Type its name.
6. Click **Close**.

To clone the Packages in the element tree

1. In the element tree, select the Package to clone. The Package is cloned recursively including all nested structures.
2. Click the **Clone** button.
3. The Specification window of cloned Package opens.
4. Type its name.
5. Click **Close**.

##### Step #3. Creating a diagram (optional)

In this step, you can choose whether you want to show your created instance specifications in a new diagram or not. If you do not wish to create a new diagram, you can simply skip this step.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To create a diagram using **Automatic Instantiation** Wizard

1. If you choose to create a new diagram for displaying instance specification(s), select the **Create a new diagram**check box.
2. If you wish to create and display links between your instance specification(s), select the **Create link between instances**check box.
3. Fill in the **Type diagram name**field by typing the diagram name. NoteBy default, the diagram name is the selected Package's name in Step 2.
4. From the **Select diagram type** drop-down list, you can select one of the diagram types.
5. Specify the owner for a new diagram:
  - Select existing Packages from the tree.
  - Click the **Create Owner** button to create a new one.
  - Click the **Clone** button to clone existing Packages.
6. After clicking the **Finish** button, a new diagram with instance specifications is created and displayed in your project.

907308985

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Automatic Instantiation Wizard Case Study' space='MD2024x']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Automatic Instantiation wizard' space='SYSMLP2024x']Automatic Instantiation wizard in SysML Plugin

When creating an instance for the <em>Vehicle</em> Class, you can change the type of the <em>engine </em>Property by selecting one of the following: <em>Engine GM</em> <span> Class, <em>Engine GMR</em> </span> <span> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Class</span>, or <em>Engine </em><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Class</span></span><span>.</span> </span></p><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="specifying_type_for_instantiated_properties.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="text-align: center;margin-bottom: 20.0px;"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Changing the type for a Part Property instance directly in the Automatic Instantiation dialog.</span></h6><h3><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Step #2. <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Selecting a package</span> </span></h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In this step, you can select the package to store instance specifications. You can select an </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">existing package from the element tree, create a new package, or clone selected </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">packages.</span> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Finish</strong> button </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">after this step if you do not want to display your created instance specifications.</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="select_package_step2.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard" /></ri:attachment></ac:image> </span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <br /> </span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To create a new Package in the element tree</span></p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the element tree, select the Package for which you want to create the new one.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Creation Mode</strong> button. </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Create Owner</strong> button.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">From the open menu, select the package kind. The Specification window of that package opens.<br /> </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Type its name.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click <strong>Close</strong>.</span></li></ol><p><br /></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To clone the Packages <span>in the element tree</span> </span></p><hr /><ol><li><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the element tree, select the Package to clone.<br /> </span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="eeb6f4cf-5cbe-45ab-9321-bf829e0ba307"><ac:rich-text-body>The Package is cloned recursively including all nested structures.</ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Clone</strong> button.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">The Specification window of cloned Package opens.<br /> </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Type its name.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click <strong>Close</strong>.</span></li></ol><h3><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Step #3. <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Creating a diagram (optional)</span> </span></h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In this step, you can choose whether you want to show your created instance specifications in a new diagram or not. If you do not wish to create a new diagram, you can simply skip this step.</span></p><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="create_diagram_step3.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <br /> </span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To create a diagram using <strong>Automatic Instantiation</strong> Wizard</span></p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">If you choose to create a new diagram for displaying instance specification(s), select the <strong>Create a new diagram </strong><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">check box</span>. </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">If you wish to create and display links between your instance specification(s), <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">select the </span> <strong>Create link between instances </strong>check box.</span></li><li><p class="auto-cursor-target"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Fill in the </span> <strong>Type diagram name </strong><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">field by typing the diagram name.<br /> </span> </span> </span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="4db12659-8cdc-4979-b226-9ee2bb0450af"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Note</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> By default, the diagram name is the selected Package's name in Step 2.<br /> </span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">From the <strong>Select diagram type</strong> drop-down list, you can select one of the diagram types.</span></li><li>Specify the owner for a new diagram:<ul><li>Select existing Packages from the tree.</li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <span>Click the <strong>Create Owner </strong></span></span>button to create a new one.</li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Clone</strong> button to clone existing Packages.</span></li></ul></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">After clicking the <strong>Finish</strong> button, a new diagram with instance specifications is created and displayed in your project. </span></li></ol></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="efee3e9e-7b4f-43e7-8821-e2cdc94040d0"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">907308985</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><strong>Related pages</strong></p><ul><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="MD2024x" ri:content-title="Automatic Instantiation Wizard Case Study" /></ac:link></li><li class="with-breadcrumbs"><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="SYSMLP2024x" ri:content-title="Automatic Instantiation wizard" /><ac:link-body><span class="current">Automatic Instantiation wizard</span> in SysML Plugin</ac:link-body></ac:link></li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro>
